<center>[img[mine]]</center>\n\n"Darling, I care about you more than anything. But that don't mean I don't care about anyone else, you know?"\n\n[[> It can't go on like this.]]
She always calls me darling when she knows I'm upset. She thinks darling makes me feel better. We met in the saloon on Colorado Ave. Buy you a drink, darling? You're a miner, aren't you. Sure am. How's about I buy you one instead. Wouldn't say no to that. Her hands were rough, but careful. And her eyes, gosh. Head over heels. Darling does make me feel better.\n\nWe go to Cripple Creek and we'll never have another problem with the bosses long as we live. That's what she told me. Ever since they split the county the union runs the show top to bottom. That's what she told me. Papers on our side sheriff on our side mayor on our side. Eight hour days four dollars a week all cash no scrip. We lived easy and worried about nothing.\n\nWe, we, we. Class solidarity, she says. I serve drinks three nights a week, where's my union? She reads all the time, she knows so much about all this, I can never tell if it's a discussion or a lecture. Sometimes I wonder if she loves the union more than she loves me.\n\nShe came home late one night. Stinking drunk, cheeks smudged soot and tears. Three hundred soldiers in Colorado City. Attacking pickets outside the mills, smashing down doors and raiding homes. Blackwell plans to wipe the workers out. It could be us next. Three hundred soldiers in Colorado City. They brought with them gatling guns. It could be us next.
